<p>Shawyer insists the EmDrive is an <a href="/wiki/Thermodynamic_system#Open_system" title="Thermodynamic system">open system</a>. However, physicists point out that relying only on special relativity, without emitting anything and with no interaction with an outside field or matter, makes his drive a <a href="/wiki/Closed_system" title="Closed system">closed system</a>. Since the two end plates are part of the thruster and the microwaves are trapped inside the cavity, standard <a href="/wiki/Einstein_field_equations#Einstein.E2.80.93Maxwell_equations" title="Einstein field equations">Einstein–Maxwell equations</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Momentum#Conservation" title="Momentum">conservation of momentum</a> show no effective thrust can occur due to any force on the cavity caused by internal electromagnetic energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vacuum_energy">Vacuum energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=RF_resonant_cavity_thruster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Vacuum energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Zero-point_energy" title="Zero-point energy">Zero-point energy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quantum_vacuum_thruster" title="Quantum vacuum thruster">Quantum vacuum thruster</a></div>
<p>Harold White, the lead scientist in the NASA investigations, suggested in 2014 that their model could be an example of a <a href="/wiki/Quantum_vacuum_thruster" title="Quantum vacuum thruster">quantum vacuum thruster</a> (QVT). This is a theoretical system that would use <a href="/wiki/Magnetohydrodynamics" title="Magnetohydrodynamics">magnetohydrodynamics</a> to generate thrust, similar to conventional <a href="/wiki/Plasma_propulsion_engine" title="Plasma propulsion engine">plasma thrusters</a>, only using the fleeting vacuum <a href="/wiki/Quantum_fluctuation" title="Quantum fluctuation">quantum fluctuations</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zero-point_field" title="Zero-point field">zero-point field</a> as an extremely low-density plasma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eagleworks_AIAA_2016_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-Eagleworks_AIAA_2016-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>White's 2016 paper states that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pilot-wave_theory" title="Pilot-wave theory">pilot-wave theories</a>, non-mainstream interpretations of quantum mechanics, may help explain how QVTs could "push off of the quantum vacuum and preserve the laws of conservation of energy and conservation of momentum.".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Quantized_inertia">Quantized inertia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=RF_resonant_cavity_thruster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Quantized inertia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A paper in <a href="/wiki/EPL_(journal)" title="EPL (journal)"><i>EPL</i></a> by Mike McCulloch, a Lecturer in <a href="/wiki/Geomatics" title="Geomatics">Geomatics</a> at <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_University" title="Plymouth University">Plymouth University</a>, describes a possible method in which thrust from resonant cavities can be predicted using McCulloch's controversial theory of quantization of inertia (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=MiHsC&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="MiHsC (page does not exist)">MiHsC</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> McCulloch hypothesizes that <a href="/wiki/Inertia" title="Inertia">inertia</a> arises from an effect predicted by <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">general relativity</a> called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unruh_radiation" title="Unruh radiation">Unruh radiation</a>, that an accelerating object experiences <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_body_radiation" title="Black body radiation">black body radiation</a>. Thus inertia is the pressure the Unruh radiation exerts on an accelerating body. At very small accelerations, Unruh wavelengths become so large they can no longer fit in the observable universe. When this happens, inertia is quantized. He pointed out possible observational evidence for this in the form of the otherwise unexplained jumps in momentum observed in some spacecraft as they <a href="/wiki/Flyby_anomaly" title="Flyby anomaly">fly past Earth toward other planets</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gadgette.com_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-gadgette.com-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> While this model allows the device to create thrust without breaking <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newton%27s_third_law" title="Newton's third law">Newton's third law</a>, it assumes that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unruh_radiation" title="Unruh radiation">Unruh radiation</a> is real, and requires the speed of light to change within the microwave cavity. This change in the speed of light is contrary to the central tenet of <a href="/wiki/Special_relativity" title="Special relativity">special relativity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Unlike some other hypotheses used to explain the device, McCulloch's hypothesis is testable and McCulloch has suggested building a cavity where the length of the cavity is the same as the diameter of the small end, to cause the Unruh radiation to fit better in the small end, resulting in a reversal of thrust.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gadgette.com_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-gadgette.com-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Photon_leakage">Photon leakage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=RF_resonant_cavity_thruster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Photon leakage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Scientists in Finland have proposed a possible explanation of this phenomenon involving the propagation of microwave <a href="/wiki/Photon" title="Photon">photons</a> leaking from the closed metal cavity and thereby producing an exhaust momentum, satisfying the classical action-reaction principle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-photon_leakage_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-photon_leakage-76">[76]</a></sup> This explanation relies on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wave-particle_duality" title="Wave-particle duality">wave-particle duality</a> of <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_radiation" title="Electromagnetic radiation">electromagnetic radiation</a>, postulating that the <a href="/wiki/Stochastic" title="Stochastic">stochastic</a> <a href="/wiki/Phase_(waves)" title="Phase (waves)">phases</a> of the microwaves will (with some <a href="/wiki/Probability" title="Probability">probability</a>) result in destructive <a href="/wiki/Interference_(wave_propagation)" title="Interference (wave propagation)">interference</a> between microwaves which cancels their electromagnetic fields but allows continued propagation of the microwave photon pairs, generating net thrust consistent with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Impulse-momentum_theorem" title="Impulse-momentum theorem">impulse-momentum theorem</a> depending on the asymmetric shape of the cavity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-photon_leakage_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-photon_leakage-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>The observed thrust of experimental results has been argued to exceed the maximum efficiency of a <a href="/wiki/Collimated_light" title="Collimated light">perfectly collimated</a> <a href="/wiki/Photon_rocket" title="Photon rocket">photon rocket</a>, comprised between 3.33 and 6.67 µN/kW.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NBF_AIAA_paper_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-NBF_AIAA_paper-80">[80]</a></sup> However, the paper follows on White's idea of a degradable quantum vacuum for effective <a href="/wiki/Pair_production" title="Pair production">pair production</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_N._Lewis" title="Gilbert N. Lewis">Lewis</a>' original concept of the photon which would be the conserved entity of nature, not its carried energy:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lewis_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis-81">[81]</a></sup> The authors argue that the environment modifies photon energy and that pairing of photons within the electromagnetic energy density gradient of a resonant cavity would cause a shift down in energy, and the loss of <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_four-potential" title="Electromagnetic four-potential">electromagnetic potential</a> becomes available for thrust, so according to the authors the level of energy of the paired photon when it escapes the cavity and the associated thrust efficiency remain an open question. The authors also argue that the cavity walls become transparent for the photon pair when it forms; as it has no associated electromagnetic field, it escapes the cavity to sparser surroundings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-photon_leakage_76-2"><a href="#cite_note-photon_leakage-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Warp_field">Warp field</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=RF_resonant_cavity_thruster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Warp field">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alcubierre.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="465" data-file-width="1004" height="102" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Alcubierre.png/220px-Alcubierre.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Alcubierre.png/330px-Alcubierre.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Alcubierre.png/440px-Alcubierre.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alcubierre.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
2D visualisation of spacetime distortion induced by the Alcubierre metric.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Warp-field_experiments" title="Warp-field experiments">Warp-field experiments</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alcubierre_drive" title="Alcubierre drive">Alcubierre drive</a></div>
<p>It has been suggested that time-varying electromagnetic energy density could produce a local gradient in the <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_potential" title="Gravitational potential">gravitational potential</a> (a distortion or warping of <a href="/wiki/Spacetime" title="Spacetime">spacetime</a>, sometimes called "warp fields"),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> as in the theoretical <a href="/wiki/Alcubierre_drive" title="Alcubierre drive">Alcubierre drive</a> or <a href="/wiki/Breakthrough_Propulsion_Physics_Program#Diametrical" title="Breakthrough Propulsion Physics Program">diametric drive</a>. Warp fields have never been observed, however they could potentially be tested using <a href="/wiki/Interferometry" title="Interferometry">interferometry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> White developed the <a href="/wiki/White%E2%80%93Juday_warp-field_interferometer" title="White–Juday warp-field interferometer">White–Juday warp-field interferometer</a> to attempt to detect such fields over short distances. His team used one to test a symmetric resonant cavity in 2013, and observed small anomalous effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> However the effects have yet to be replicated on an asymmetric cavity, or in a vacuum to prevent interference from the heating of surrounding air.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>Physicist Fernando Minotti, building on work by <a href="/wiki/Matt_Visser" title="Matt Visser">Matt Visser</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lobo-Visser_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lobo-Visser-86">[86]</a></sup> estimated the forces on asymmetric electromagnetic resonant cavities using <a href="/wiki/Brans%E2%80%93Dicke_theory" title="Brans–Dicke theory">Brans–Dicke theory</a>, an alternate framework for describing gravity that competes with <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">general relativity</a>. In Minoti's model, thrust results from gravitational forces on the cavity walls, with some <a href="/wiki/Scalar_field" title="Scalar field">scalar coupling field</a> providing an effective negative energy source.</p>
<p>Minotti suggested that this model implies the direction of the force produced by a tapered resonant cavity would be dependent on its <a href="/wiki/Normal_mode" title="Normal mode">resonant mode</a>, and the thrust magnitude would increase with the thickness and mass of the material the cavity is made of.</p>
<p>However, Minotti noted that Brans–Dicke theory is not accepted by the majority of the scientific community, and that his linear model also predicts large gravitational effects due to the <a href="/wiki/Earth%27s_magnetic_field" title="Earth's magnetic field">Earth's magnetic field</a> which have not been observed. He hypothesized that some nonlinear version of his model might provide a framework which does not predict such unreal effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Minotti_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Minotti-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>After Yang retracted her previous high power results,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yang_2016_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-Yang_2016-7">[7]</a></sup> Minotti completed a revaluation of the scalar-tensor theory fixing some inconsistencies. The equations are now derived without ad hoc conditions and <a href="/wiki/Maxwell%27s_equations" title="Maxwell's equations">Maxwell's equations</a> are obtained in the <a href="/wiki/Linearized_gravity#Weak-field_approximation" title="Linearized gravity">weak field approximation</a> with no unreal prediction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NBF_20160501_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-NBF_20160501-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Minotti2_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Minotti2-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Propellantless_or_reactionless_drive">Propellantless or reactionless drive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=RF_resonant_cavity_thruster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Propellantless or reactionless drive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Reactionless_drive" title="Reactionless drive">Reactionless drive</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Propellantless_drive" title="Propellantless drive">Propellantless drive</a></div>
<p>If the thrust produced by the RF resonant cavity thruster is due to an interaction with an external <a href="/wiki/Field_(physics)" title="Field (physics)">field</a>, it is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Propellantless_drive" title="Propellantless drive">propellantless drive</a> constituting an <a href="/wiki/Thermodynamic_system#Open_system" title="Thermodynamic system">open system</a> that does not violate any physical law, for example like a conventional spacecraft accelerating at the expense of the momentum of the planet it orbits during a <a href="/wiki/Gravity_assist" title="Gravity assist">gravity assist maneuver</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slingshot_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-slingshot-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>However true reactionless drives as <a href="/wiki/Closed_system" title="Closed system">closed systems</a> are considered impossible for many reasons. For example, most are a form of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perpetual_motion_machine" title="Perpetual motion machine">perpetual motion machine</a>. If thrust were produced without expelling momentum from the system in the opposite direction, the lack of momentum expulsion would make the device not only propellantless, but also reactionless, in the sense of violating <a href="/wiki/Newton%27s_laws_of_motion#Newton.27s_3rd_Law" title="Newton's laws of motion">Newton's Third Law</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conservation_of_momentum" title="Conservation of momentum">conservation of momentum</a>. Any such drive would require a new undiscovered physical law, which somehow had not been observed under any other conditions. The experimenters that have studied resonant cavity thrusters generally do not believe the drives are reactionless, and are trying to test one of the alternative hypotheses.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="all serious scientific proposals state that the RF cavity is an open system, who argues it is a closed system AND works? (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Finally, one case of a true reactionless drive as an open system, exchanging no momentum with the outside but still producing motion without violating physical laws, would be a device distorting spacetime, creating a gravitational potential like a relativistic <a href="/wiki/Alcubierre_drive" title="Alcubierre drive">Alcubierre drive</a> or a low-velocity <a href="/wiki/Warp_drive" title="Warp drive">warp drive</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lobo-Visser_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lobo-Visser-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Testing_and_replication">Testing and replication</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=RF_resonant_cavity_thruster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Testing and replication">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tests_by_the_inventors">Tests by the inventors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=RF_resonant_cavity_thruster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Tests by the inventors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2004, Roger Shawyer reported seven independent positive reviews from experts at <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems" title="BAE Systems">BAE Systems</a>, <a href="/wiki/Astrium" title="Astrium">EADS Astrium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Institution_of_Electrical_Engineers" title="Institution of Electrical Engineers">IEE</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Engineer_2004_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Engineer_2004-90">[90]</a></sup> however these are disputed. In a letter to <i>New Scientist</i>, the then-technical director of EADS Astrium (Shawyer's former employer) denied this, stating</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"I reviewed Roger’s work and concluded that both theory and experiment were fatally flawed. Roger was advised that the company had no interest in the device, did not wish to seek patent coverage and in fact did not wish to be associated with it in any way."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newscientist-astrium-debunk_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-newscientist-astrium-debunk-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>In 2011, Fetta tested a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Superconductor" title="Superconductor">superconducting</a> version of the Cannae drive. The RF resonant cavity was suspended inside a liquid helium-filled <a href="/wiki/Vacuum_flask" title="Vacuum flask">dewar</a>. The weight of the cavity was monitored by <a href="/wiki/Load_cell" title="Load cell">load cells</a>. Fetta theorized that when the device was activated and produced upward thrust, the load cells would detect the thrust as change in weight. When the drive was energized by sending 10.5 watt power pulses of RF power into the resonant cavity, there was, as predicted, a reduction in compressive force on the load cells consistent with thrust of 8-10 mN.</p>
<p>None of these results have been published in the scientific literature, or replicated by independent researchers. They have been posted on their inventors' websites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, Shawyer published an article in <i><a href="/wiki/Acta_Astronautica" title="Acta Astronautica">Acta Astronautica</a></i>, summarising existing tests on the EmDrive. Of seven tests, four produced a measured force in the intended direction and three produced thrust in the opposite direction. Furthermore, in one test, thrust could be produced in either direction by varying the spring constants in the measuring apparatus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Northwestern_Polytechnical_University">Northwestern Polytechnical University</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=RF_resonant_cavity_thruster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Northwestern Polytechnical University">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2008, a team of Chinese researchers led by Juan Yang (杨涓), professor of propulsion theory and engineering of aeronautics and astronautics at <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Polytechnical_University" title="Northwestern Polytechnical University">Northwestern Polytechnical University</a> (NWPU) in <a href="/wiki/Xi%27an" title="Xi'an">Xi'an</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shaanxi" title="Shaanxi">Shaanxi</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, said that they had developed a valid electro-magnetic theory behind a microwave resonant cavity thruster.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wired_2008_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wired_2008-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yang_2008_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yang_2008-93">[93]</a></sup> A demonstration version of the drive was built and tested with different cavity shapes and at higher power levels in 2010. Using an aerospace <a href="/wiki/Engine_test_stand" title="Engine test stand">engine test stand</a> usually used to precisely test spacecraft engines like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ion_drive" title="Ion drive">ion drives</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wired_2013_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-Wired_2013-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yang_2013_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-Yang_2013-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yang_2014_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-Yang_2014-43">[43]</a></sup> they reported a maximum thrust of 720 mN at 2,500 W of input power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yang_2014_43-2"><a href="#cite_note-Yang_2014-43">[43]</a></sup> Yang noted that her results were tentative, and said she "[was] not able to discuss her work until more results are published".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wired_2013_5-5"><a href="#cite_note-Wired_2013-5">[5]</a></sup> This positive result was over 100x more thrust per input power than any other experiment, and inspired other groups to try to replicate their work. However in a followup paper, Yang could not reproduce the 2010 observation and suggested it was due to experimental error.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yang_2016_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-Yang_2016-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2016, Yang's team published a paper, in which they refined their experimental setup, using a three-wire torsion pendulum to measure thrust. They tested two different power setups. In one trial, the power system was outside the cavity: in this case, they observed a "thrust" of 8-10 mN. In a second trial, the power system was within the cavity, and they measured no such thrust. Instead they observed an insignificant thrust below their noise threshold of 3 mN, fluctuating between ±0.7 mN with a measurement uncertainty of 80%. They concluded that they were unable to measure significant thrust; that "thrust" measured when using external power sources (as in their 2010 experiment) could be noise; and that it was important to use self-contained power systems for these experiments, and more sensitive pendulums with lower <a href="/wiki/Torsion_constant" title="Torsion constant">torsional</a> <a href="/wiki/Stiffness" title="Stiffness">stiffness</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yang_2016_7-4"><a href="#cite_note-Yang_2016-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="NASA_Eagleworks">NASA Eagleworks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=RF_resonant_cavity_thruster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: NASA Eagleworks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since 2011, <a href="/wiki/Harold_G._White" title="Harold G. White">White</a> has had a team at NASA known as the <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Propulsion_Physics_Laboratory" title="Advanced Propulsion Physics Laboratory">Advanced Propulsion Physics Laboratory</a>, or Eagleworks Laboratories, which is devoted to studying exotic propulsion concepts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eagleworks_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eagleworks-94">[94]</a></sup> The group has investigated ideas for a wide range of untested and <a href="/wiki/Fringe_science" title="Fringe science">fringe proposals</a>, including <a href="/wiki/IXS_Enterprise" title="IXS Enterprise">Alcubierre drives</a>, drives that interact with the <a href="/wiki/Quantum_vacuum_thruster" title="Quantum vacuum thruster">quantum vacuum</a>, and RF resonant cavity thrusters.</p>
<p>In 2014, the group began testing resonant cavity thrusters of their own design and sharing some of their results. In November 2016, they published their first peer-reviewed paper on this work, in the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Journal_of_Propulsion_and_Power" title="Journal of Propulsion and Power">Journal of Propulsion and Power</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eagleworks_AIAA_2016_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-Eagleworks_AIAA_2016-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hacked_18112016_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hacked_18112016-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forbes_peer_review_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes_peer_review-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wired_Peer_review_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wired_Peer_review-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Motherboard_Peer_Review_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Motherboard_Peer_Review-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="EmDrive_and_tapered_cavities">EmDrive and tapered cavities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=RF_resonant_cavity_thruster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: EmDrive and tapered cavities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In July 2014, Eagleworks reported tentative positive results for evaluating a tapered RF resonant cavity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_AIAA_2014_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-NASA_AIAA_2014-22">[22]</a></sup> Testing was performed using a low-thrust <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Torsion_pendulum" title="Torsion pendulum">torsion pendulum</a> able to detect force at the µN level within a sealed but unevacuated <a href="/wiki/Vacuum_chamber" title="Vacuum chamber">vacuum chamber</a> (the <a href="/wiki/RF_power_amplifier" title="RF power amplifier">RF power amplifier</a> used an <a href="/wiki/Electrolytic_capacitor" title="Electrolytic capacitor">electrolytic capacitor</a> unable to operate in a hard vacuum).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_AIAA_2014_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-NASA_AIAA_2014-22">[22]</a></sup> The experimenters recorded directional thrust immediately upon application of power.</p>
<p>Their first tests of this tapered cavity were conducted at very low power (2% of Shawyer's 2002 experiment). A net mean thrust over five runs was measured at 91.2 µN at 17 W of input power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_AIAA_2014_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-NASA_AIAA_2014-22">[22]</a></sup> The experiment was criticized for its small data set and for not having been conducted in vacuum, to eliminate thermal air currents.</p>
<p>The group announced a plan to upgrade their equipment to higher power levels, to use vacuum-capable RF amplifiers with power ranges of up to 125 W, and to design a new tapered cavity that could be in the 0.1 N/kW range. The test article was to be subject to independent <a href="/wiki/Verification_and_validation" title="Verification and validation">verification and validation</a> at <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Research_Center" title="Glenn Research Center">Glenn Research Center</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">Jet Propulsion Laboratory</a> and the Johns Hopkins University <a href="/wiki/Applied_Physics_Laboratory" title="Applied Physics Laboratory">Applied Physics Laboratory</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_AIAA_2014_22-4"><a href="#cite_note-NASA_AIAA_2014-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NBF_20150206_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-NBF_20150206-99">[99]</a></sup> As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=RF_resonant_cavity_thruster&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, this validation has not happened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, Paul March from Eagleworks made new results public, measured with a torsional pendulum in a hard vacuum: about 50 µN with 50 W of input power at 5.0×10<sup>−6</sup> <a href="/wiki/Torr" title="Torr">torr</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NBF_20150206_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-NBF_20150206-99">[99]</a></sup> The new RF power amplifiers were said to be made for hard vacuum, but failed rapidly due to internal <a href="/wiki/Corona_discharge" title="Corona discharge">corona discharges</a>. Without funding to replace or upgrade them, measurements were scarce for a time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NBF_20150207_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-NBF_20150207-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>They conducted further experiments in vacuum, a set of 18 observations with 40-80W of input power. They published the results in the <a href="/wiki/American_Institute_of_Aeronautics_and_Astronautics" title="American Institute of Aeronautics and Astronautics">American Institute of Aeronautics and Astronautics</a>'s peer-reviewed <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Journal_of_Propulsion_and_Power" title="Journal of Propulsion and Power">Journal of Propulsion and Power</a></i>, under the title <i>"Measurement of Impulsive Thrust from a Closed Radio-Frequency Cavity in Vacuum"</i>. This was released online in November 2016, with print publication in December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eagleworks_AIAA_2016_9-4"><a href="#cite_note-Eagleworks_AIAA_2016-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forbes_peer_review_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes_peer_review-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wired_Peer_review_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wired_Peer_review-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Motherboard_Peer_Review_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-Motherboard_Peer_Review-98">[98]</a></sup> The study said that the system was "consistently performing with a thrust-to-power ratio of 1.2±0.1mN/kW", and enumerated many potential sources of error.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eagleworks_AIAA_2016_9-5"><a href="#cite_note-Eagleworks_AIAA_2016-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The paper suggested that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pilot-wave_theory" title="Pilot-wave theory">pilot-wave theory</a> (a controversial, non-mainstream deterministic interpretation of quantum mechanics) could explain how the device produces thrust.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eagleworks_AIAA_2016_9-6"><a href="#cite_note-Eagleworks_AIAA_2016-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wired_Peer_review_97-2"><a href="#cite_note-Wired_Peer_review-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Motherboard_Peer_Review_98-2"><a href="#cite_note-Motherboard_Peer_Review-98">[98]</a></sup> Commenters pointed out that just because a study reporting consistent thrust was published with peer-review does not necessarily mean that the drive functions as claimed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nat_Geo_Peer_review_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-Nat_Geo_Peer_review-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forbes_peer_review_96-2"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes_peer_review-96">[96]</a></sup> Physicist Ethan Siegal commented on the paper, saying that the drive most likely does not violate conservation of momentum as this would "make physics fall apart" but rather that there is something else going on. He said that "Whether it’s new physics [or] the effect’s cause simply hasn’t been determined yet, more and better experiments will be the ultimate arbiter".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forbes_ES_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes_ES-102">[102]</a></sup> Physicist Chris Lee was very critical of the work, saying that the paper had a small data set and a number of missing details he described as 'gaping holes'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chris_Lee_Ars_Technica_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chris_Lee_Ars_Technica-103">[103]</a></sup> Electrical Engineer George Hathaway analyzed and criticized the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_method" title="Scientific method">scientific method</a> described in the paper.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tau_Zero_2_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tau_Zero_2-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cannae_drive">Cannae drive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=RF_resonant_cavity_thruster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cannae drive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>White's 2014 tests also evaluated two Cannae drive prototypes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_AIAA_2014_22-5"><a href="#cite_note-NASA_AIAA_2014-22">[22]</a></sup> One had radial slots engraved along the bottom rim of the resonant cavity interior, as required by Fetta's theory to produce thrust;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cannae_LLC_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cannae_LLC-37">[37]</a></sup> another "null" test article lacked those radial slots. Both drives were equipped with an internal <a href="/wiki/Dielectric" title="Dielectric">dielectric</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_AIAA_2014_22-6"><a href="#cite_note-NASA_AIAA_2014-22">[22]</a></sup> A third test article, the experimental control, had an RF load but no resonant cavity interior. These tests took place at atmospheric pressure.</p>
<p>About the same net thrust was reported for both the device with radial slots and the device without slots. Thrust was not reported for the experimental control. Some considered the positive result for the non-slotted device a possible flaw in the experiment, as the null test device had been expected to produce less or no thrust based upon Fetta's theory of how thrust was produced by the device.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Powell_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-Powell-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ars_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ars-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> In the complete paper, however, Eagleworks concluded that the test results proved that "thrust production was not dependent upon slotting".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_AIAA_2014_22-7"><a href="#cite_note-NASA_AIAA_2014-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dresden_University_of_Technology">Dresden University of Technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=RF_resonant_cavity_thruster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Dresden University of Technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In July 2015 an aerospace research group at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dresden_University_of_Technology" title="Dresden University of Technology">Dresden University of Technology</a> (TUD) under <a href="/wiki/Martin_Tajmar" title="Martin Tajmar">Martin Tajmar</a> reported results for an evaluation of an RF resonant tapered cavity similar to the EmDrive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tajmar2015_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tajmar2015-107">[107]</a></sup> Testing was performed first on a knife-edge <a href="/wiki/Weighing_scale" title="Weighing scale">beam balance</a> able to detect force at the µN level, atop an antivibration granite table at ambient air pressure; then on a torsion pendulum with a force resolution of 0.1 mN, inside a vacuum chamber at ambient air pressure and in a hard vacuum at 4×10<sup>−6</sup> mbar (3×10<sup>−6</sup> torr).</p>
<p>They used a conventional <a href="/wiki/ISM_band" title="ISM band">ISM band</a> 2.45 GHz 700 W oven magnetron, and a small cavity with a low Q factor (20 in vacuum tests). They observed small positive thrusts in the positive direction and negative thrusts in the negative direction, of about 20 µN in a hard vacuum. However when they rotated the cavity upwards as a "null" configuration, they observed an anomalous thrust of hundreds of µN, significantly larger than the expected result of zero thrust. This indicated a strong source of noise which they could not identify. This led them to conclude that they could not confirm or refute claims about such a thruster. At the time they considered future experiments with better magnetic shielding, other vacuum tests and improved cavities with higher <i>Q</i> factors.</p>
<p>Eric W. Davis, a physicist at the Institute for Advanced Studies at Austin, noted "The experiment is quite detailed but no theoretical account for momentum violation is given by Tajmar, which will cause peer reviews and technical journal editors to reject his paper should it be submitted to any of the peer-review physics and aerospace journals."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-:0-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tests_in_space">Tests in space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=RF_resonant_cavity_thruster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Tests in space">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In November 2016 the <i><a href="/wiki/International_Business_Times" title="International Business Times">International Business Times</a></i> claimed the U.S. government was testing a version of the EmDrive on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boeing_X-37B" title="Boeing X-37B">Boeing X-37B</a> and that the Chinese government has made plans to incorporate the EmDrive on its orbital space laboratory <a href="/wiki/Tiangong-2" title="Tiangong-2">Tiangong-2</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibtimes20161107_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-ibtimes20161107-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avion20161114_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-avion20161114-109">[109]</a></sup> In 2009 an EmDrive technology transfer contract with Boeing was undertaken via a State Department TAA and a UK export licence, approved by the UK MOD. The appropriate US government agencies including DARPA, USAF and NSSO were aware of the contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shawyer2015_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shawyer2015-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> However, prior to flight, the propulsion experiment aboard the X-37B was officially announced as a test of a <a href="/wiki/Hall-effect_thruster" title="Hall-effect thruster">Hall-effect thruster</a> built by <a href="/wiki/Aerojet_Rocketdyne" title="Aerojet Rocketdyne">Aerojet Rocketdyne</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfn20150427_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-sfn20150427-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Chinese tests reported by the <i>International Business Times</i> report were later corroborated; at a press conference in Beijing on 10 December 2016 at the <a href="/wiki/China_Academy_of_Space_Technology" title="China Academy of Space Technology">China Academy of Space Technology</a> (CAST), Yue Chen, head of the communication satellite division at CAST, confirmed the agency is already testing an EmDrive in low-Earth orbit onboard an "experimental verification platform" believed to be the Tiangong-2 space station, and that it has been funding research in the area for the last five years. It stated that the current prototype generates only a few millinewtons of thrust, and that it will have to be scaled up to at least 100-1000 millinewtons; despite this they currently plan to add the technology to Chinese satellites as soon as possible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibtimes20161213_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-ibtimes20161213-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibtimes20161214_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-ibtimes20161214-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stdaily20161211_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-stdaily20161211-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopSci_20161220_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-PopSci_20161220-46">[46]</a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-GrahnAnnila2016-47"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-GrahnAnnila2016_47-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Grahn, Patrick; Annila, Arto; Kolehmainen, Erkki (2016). <a class="external text" href="http://scitation.aip.org/docserver/fulltext/aip/journal/adva/6/6/1.4953807.pdf?expires=1480693477&amp;id=id&amp;accname=guest&amp;checksum=36CF1623E0E8BCA1ECF6B6639E526D66" rel="nofollow">"On the exhaust of electromagnetic drive"</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span>. <i>AIP Advances</i>. <b>6</b> (6): 065205. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//dx.doi.org/10.1063%2F1.4953807" rel="nofollow">10.1063/1.4953807</a>. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Serial_Number" title="International Standard Serial Number">ISSN</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/issn/2158-3226" rel="nofollow">2158-3226</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARF+resonant+cavity+thruster&amp;rft.atitle=On+the+exhaust+of+electromagnetic+drive&amp;rft.au=Annila%2C+Arto&amp;rft.aufirst=Patrick&amp;rft.au=Kolehmainen%2C+Erkki&amp;rft.aulast=Grahn&amp;rft.date=2016&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fscitation.aip.org%2Fdocserver%2Ffulltext%2Faip%2Fjournal%2Fadva%2F6%2F6%2F1.4953807.pdf%3Fexpires%3D1480693477%26id%3Did%26accname%3Dguest%26checksum%3D36CF1623E0E8BCA1ECF6B6639E526D66&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1063%2F1.4953807&amp;rft.issn=2158-3226&amp;rft.issue=6&amp;rft.jtitle=AIP+Advances&amp;rft.pages=065205&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=6"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-48"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-48">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Davis, A.M.J.; Scharstein, R.W. (1994). <a class="external text" href="http://scharstein.eng.ua.edu/electromagnetic.pdf" rel="nofollow">"Electromagnetic plane wave excitation of an open-ended conducting frustum"</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span>. <i>IEEE Transactions on Antennas and Propagation</i>. <b>42</b> (5): 699–706. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//dx.doi.org/10.1109%2F8.299569" rel="nofollow">10.1109/8.299569</a>. <q>Therefore real nonzero time-average power flow does occur in a conical waveguide that is smaller in cross section then any cut-on circular wave guide at the same frequency of operation. This observation can be qualitatively explained by considering the oppositely directed evanescent waves that are excited at the cascaded junctions of successively larger but still individually cut off circular waveguides that form a stepped approximation to the cone. Effectively, then, the conical scatterer tends to focus a portion of energy of the incident portion of the radio wave, at least in comparison to the uniform tubular scatterer... In most respects, the scattering by the frustum is a distortion of that by the circular tube. One important difference is the internal focusing effect that is predominantly experienced when the exciting plane wave is incident from the wide end of the frustum. Due to the absence of sharp cut off frequencies from the nonuniform conical waveguide, the interior of the frustum can support nontrivial field amplitudes, even in regions of relatively small electrical cross section.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARF+resonant+cavity+thruster&amp;rft.atitle=Electromagnetic+plane+wave+excitation+of+an+open-ended+conducting+frustum&amp;rft.aufirst=A.M.J.&amp;rft.aulast=Davis&amp;rft.au=Scharstein%2C+R.W.&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fscharstein.eng.ua.edu%2Felectromagnetic.pdf&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1109%2F8.299569&amp;rft.issue=5&amp;rft.jtitle=IEEE+Transactions+on+Antennas+and+Propagation&amp;rft.pages=699-706&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=42"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-49"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-49">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Zeng, Xiahui; Fan, Dianyuan (2008). <a class="external text" href="https://www.osapublishing.org/DirectPDFAccess/82D470C0-ADA0-DC3F-8FE3629C1E167766_175583/oe-17-1-34.pdf?da=1&amp;id=175583&amp;seq=0&amp;mobile=no" rel="nofollow">"Electromagnetic fields and transmission properties in tapered hollow metallic waveguides"</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span>. <i>Optics Express</i>. <b>17</b> (1): 34. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//dx.doi.org/10.1364%2FOE.17.000034" rel="nofollow">10.1364/OE.17.000034</a>. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Serial_Number" title="International Standard Serial Number">ISSN</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/issn/1094-4087" rel="nofollow">1094-4087</a>. <q>It is shown that all modes run continuously from a propagating through a transition to an evanescent region and the value of the attenuation increases as the distance from the cone vertex and the cone angle decreases. A strict distinction between pure propagating and pure evanescent modes can not be achieved. There is no well-defined cutoff wavelength but rather a cutoff radius. It is interesting to note that the magnitude of the cutoff radius is related to the wavelength and the cone half-angle.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARF+resonant+cavity+thruster&amp;rft.atitle=Electromagnetic+fields+and+transmission+properties+in+tapered+hollow+metallic+waveguides&amp;rft.au=Fan%2C+Dianyuan&amp;rft.aufirst=Xiahui&amp;rft.aulast=Zeng&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.osapublishing.org%2FDirectPDFAccess%2F82D470C0-ADA0-DC3F-8FE3629C1E167766_175583%2Foe-17-1-34.pdf%3Fda%3D1%26id%3D175583%26seq%3D0%26mobile%3Dno&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1364%2FOE.17.000034&amp;rft.issn=1094-4087&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.jtitle=Optics+Express&amp;rft.pages=34&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=17"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-50">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Mayer, B.; Reccius, A.; Knochel, R. (1992). "Conical cavity for surface resistance measurements of high temperature superconductors". <i>IEEE Transactions on Microwave Theory and Techniques</i>. <b>40</b> (2): 228–236. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//dx.doi.org/10.1109%2F22.120094" rel="nofollow">10.1109/22.120094</a>. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Serial_Number" title="International Standard Serial Number">ISSN</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/issn/0018-9480" rel="nofollow">0018-9480</a>. <q>A conical cavity is described. The new cavity is superior to the often used cylindrical cavity, because it intrinsically does not suffer from mode degeneration</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARF+resonant+cavity+thruster&amp;rft.atitle=Conical+cavity+for+surface+resistance+measurements+of+high+temperature+superconductors&amp;rft.aufirst=B.&amp;rft.au=Knochel%2C+R.&amp;rft.aulast=Mayer&amp;rft.au=Reccius%2C+A.&amp;rft.date=1992&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1109%2F22.120094&amp;rft.issn=0018-9480&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.jtitle=IEEE+Transactions+on+Microwave+Theory+and+Techniques&amp;rft.pages=228-236&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=40"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-51">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">White, Harold; March, Paul; Lawrence, James; Vera, Jerry; Sylvester, Andre; Brady, David; Bailey, Paul (2016). <a class="external text" href="http://arc.aiaa.org/doi/pdf/10.2514/1.B36120" rel="nofollow">"Measurement of Impulsive Thrust from a Closed Radio-Frequency Cavity in Vacuum"</a>. <i>Journal of Propulsion and Power</i>. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//dx.doi.org/10.2514%2F1.B36120" rel="nofollow">10.2514/1.B36120</a>. <q>A 13.5-mm-diam loop antenna drives the system in the TM212 mode at 1937 MHz. Because there are no analytical solutions for the resonant modes of a truncated cone, the use of the term TM212 describes a mode with two nodes in the axial direction and four nodes in the azimuthal direction</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARF+resonant+cavity+thruster&amp;rft.atitle=Measurement+of+Impulsive+Thrust+from+a+Closed+Radio-Frequency+Cavity+in+Vacuum&amp;rft.au=Bailey%2C+Paul&amp;rft.au=Brady%2C+David&amp;rft.aufirst=Harold&amp;rft.aulast=White&amp;rft.au=Lawrence%2C+James&amp;rft.au=March%2C+Paul&amp;rft.au=Sylvester%2C+Andre&amp;rft.au=Vera%2C+Jerry&amp;rft.date=2016&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Farc.aiaa.org%2Fdoi%2Fpdf%2F10.2514%2F1.B36120&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.2514%2F1.B36120&amp;rft.jtitle=Journal+of+Propulsion+and+Power&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-Cullen_1952-65"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Cullen_1952_65-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Cullen, A. L. (April 1952). "Absolute power measurement at microwave frequencies". <i>Proceedings of the IEE Part IV: Institution Monographs</i>. <b>99</b> (2): 100–111. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//dx.doi.org/10.1049%2Fpi-4.1952.0012" rel="nofollow">10.1049/pi-4.1952.0012</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARF+resonant+cavity+thruster&amp;rft.atitle=Absolute+power+measurement+at+microwave+frequencies&amp;rft.aufirst=A.+L.&amp;rft.aulast=Cullen&amp;rft.date=1952-04&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1049%2Fpi-4.1952.0012&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.jtitle=Proceedings+of+the+IEE+Part+IV%3A+Institution+Monographs&amp;rft.pages=100-111&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=99"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-66"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-66">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Daniel Oberhaus (14 November 2016). <a class="external text" href="http://motherboard.vice.com/read/the-fact-and-fiction-of-the-nasa-emdrive-paper-leak" rel="nofollow">"The Fact and Fiction of the NASA EmDrive Paper Leak"</a>. <i>Motherboard</i>. <q>Another leading explanation is that the EmDrive’s thrust is generated by radiation pressure, a position held by its inventor Roger Shawyer. […] Yet, according to Woodward, both of these theories are unlikely to be correct for a simple reason: Physics doesn’t allow them. By way of example, Woodward likened explaining the results seen at NASA purely in terms of microwave pressure to arguing that you can accelerate a car by getting in the driver’s seat and pushing on the windshield. <i>Can any disposition of microwaves inside the cavity produce thrust?</i> said Woodward. <i>There's a simple answer to that question: No, it cannot. Conservation of momentum dictates that any purely electromagnetic system that is enclosed cannot produce thrust. This is for both quantum theory and classical electrodynamics. It's physically impossible.</i></q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARF+resonant+cavity+thruster&amp;rft.atitle=The+Fact+and+Fiction+of+the+NASA+EmDrive+Paper+Leak&amp;rft.au=Daniel+Oberhaus&amp;rft.date=2016-11-14&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fmotherboard.vice.com%2Fread%2Fthe-fact-and-fiction-of-the-nasa-emdrive-paper-leak&amp;rft.jtitle=Motherboard&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-85"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-85">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Rodal, José; Mullikin, Jeremiah; Noel, Munson (29 April 2015). <a class="external text" href="https://www.nasaspaceflight.com/2015/04/evaluating-nasas-futuristic-em-drive/" rel="nofollow">"Evaluating NASA's Futuristic EM Drive"</a>. <i>NASASpaceFlight</i>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARF+resonant+cavity+thruster&amp;rft.atitle=Evaluating+NASA%27s+Futuristic+EM+Drive&amp;rft.aufirst=Jos%C3%A9&amp;rft.aulast=Rodal&amp;rft.au=Mullikin%2C+Jeremiah&amp;rft.au=Noel%2C+Munson&amp;rft.date=2015-04-29&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.nasaspaceflight.com%2F2015%2F04%2Fevaluating-nasas-futuristic-em-drive%2F&amp;rft.jtitle=NASASpaceFlight&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Lobo-Visser-86"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Lobo-Visser_86-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Lobo-Visser_86-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Lobo, F.S.N.; Visser, M. (25 November 2004). "Fundamental limitations on 'warp drive' spacetimes". <i>Classical and Quantum Gravity</i>. <b>21</b> (24): 5871. <a href="/wiki/ArXiv" title="ArXiv">arXiv</a>:<span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="//arxiv.org/abs/gr-qc/0406083" rel="nofollow">gr-qc/0406083</a><span style="margin-left:0.1em"><img alt="Freely accessible" data-file-height="813" data-file-width="512" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Lock-green.svg/9px-Lock-green.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Lock-green.svg/14px-Lock-green.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Lock-green.svg/18px-Lock-green.svg.png 2x" title="Freely accessible" width="9"/></span></span>. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//dx.doi.org/10.1088%2F0264-9381%2F21%2F24%2F011" rel="nofollow">10.1088/0264-9381/21/24/011</a>. <q>Certain classical systems (such as non-minimally coupled scalar fields) have been found that violate the null and the weak energy conditions. […] We will take the bubble velocity to be non-relativistic, <i>v</i> ≪ 1. Thus we are not focussing attention on the "superluminal" aspects of the warp bubble, […] but rather on a secondary unremarked effect: The warp drive (if it can be realised in nature) appears to be an example of a "reaction-less drive" wherein the warp bubble moves by interacting with the geometry of spacetime instead of expending reaction mass.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARF+resonant+cavity+thruster&amp;rft.atitle=Fundamental+limitations+on+%27warp+drive%27+spacetimes&amp;rft.aufirst=F.S.N.&amp;rft.aulast=Lobo&amp;rft.au=Visser%2C+M.&amp;rft.date=2004-11-25&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=info%3Aarxiv%2Fgr-qc%2F0406083&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1088%2F0264-9381%2F21%2F24%2F011&amp;rft.issue=24&amp;rft.jtitle=Classical+and+Quantum+Gravity&amp;rft.pages=5871&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=21"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Minotti-87"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Minotti_87-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Minotti, F. O. (July 2013). "Scalar-tensor theories and asymmetric resonant cavities". <i>Gravitation and Cosmology</i>. <b>19</b> (3): 201–208. <a href="/wiki/ArXiv" title="ArXiv">arXiv</a>:<span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="//arxiv.org/abs/1302.5690" rel="nofollow">1302.5690</a><span style="margin-left:0.1em"><img alt="Freely accessible" data-file-height="813" data-file-width="512" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Lock-green.svg/9px-Lock-green.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Lock-green.svg/14px-Lock-green.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Lock-green.svg/18px-Lock-green.svg.png 2x" title="Freely accessible" width="9"/></span></span>. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//dx.doi.org/10.1134%2FS0202289313030080" rel="nofollow">10.1134/S0202289313030080</a>. <q>It appears that General Relativity might allow for such kind of reactionless propulsion, as exemplified and noted for the first time [by Lobo &amp; Visser], where the low velocity limit of some warp drive spacetimes was analyzed. As indicated there, negative energy densities are required to accomplish that and, notably, some scalar fields present this possibility. […] The lowest mode (ν= 1.05 GHz) leads to a force much larger in magnitude and of opposite direction to that of the next two modes. This and other dependencies of the predicted force, as the proportionality to the cavity wall thickness […] can be explored experimentally with relative ease to test the theory.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARF+resonant+cavity+thruster&amp;rft.atitle=Scalar-tensor+theories+and+asymmetric+resonant+cavities&amp;rft.aufirst=F.+O.&amp;rft.aulast=Minotti&amp;rft.date=2013-07&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=info%3Aarxiv%2F1302.5690&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1134%2FS0202289313030080&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.jtitle=Gravitation+and+Cosmology&amp;rft.pages=201-208&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=19"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
